Have students identify
George Washington
and explain what the
Revolutionary War was.



Lesson 9 Robert E. Lee
**147**


Support


_Refuse_ means to say
no to.



**Show Image 9A-4: Jefferson Davis’s Cabinet**
**with Lee**


At first, Lee refused to join the Confederate
Army when President Jefferson Davis asked
him to take command. ~~_Remember, Jefferson_~~
~~_Davis was elected president of the Confederacy._~~
~~_He is the man in the image who is seated with_~~
~~_a paper in his hand._~~ Then, just before the
Battle of Fort Sumter, President Lincoln asked Lee if he would agree to take
command of the entire Union Army. Lee refused that offer, as well. ~~_Why do you_~~
~~_think General Lee refused both offers?_~~ Only when his home state of Virginia
decided to secede and join the Confederacy did Lee finally make up his mind.


He hated the thought of fighting against the United States, but he hated the
thought of fighting against his home state of Virginia even more.


General Lee became Commander of the Army of Northern Virginia, making him
one of the most powerful and recognizable figures in the Confederate Army. This
image shows Confederate President Jefferson Davis and his closest **advisors**,
including General Lee in the middle, discussing their war plan. ~~[Point out Jefferson~~
~~Davis and Robert E. Lee.] Advisors~~ ~~_are people who give suggestions or guidance to_~~
~~_someone._~~ Thanks in large part to General Lee’s excellent abilities as a general, he
commanded the Confederate Army to many victories in major battles on the field
before Gettysburg. But still, there was no end to the war in sight.


**Show Image 9A-5: Lee Telling Venable His**
**Plan**


There was a knock on General Lee’s door
in Gettysburg. It was Major Venable, Lee’s
trusted friend and aide, ~~_or helper_~~ . “General,
I have reports from your field commanders,”
said Major Venable.


“Go ahead,” he said, turning his attention back to the maps on the table.


“General Ewell had trouble organizing his men, sir, and General Rodes failed to
attack as ordered. General Early tried, but he gave up as darkness approached.”


Lee tapped his knuckles on the table and stared at the maps. There had been
nothing but bad news all day. After two days of fighting, the Union Army held
the high ground, its soldiers and cannons spread in a tight line atop a long ridge,
refusing to budge. The Union Army was on higher ground than the Confederate
Army, so they had a better position and ability to see. “I have made my decision,”



Unit 7 The U.S. Civil War
**148**


Lee said. “We will strike at the heart of the Union line, at Cemetery Ridge, and
divide their forces. Then the rest of our army will attack on the left and right.”


**Show Image 9A-6: Lee Greeting His Soldiers**


In the morning, The Old Man rode out to greet
his soldiers.


The men cheered and waved their hats
whenever Lee rode past, and he waved and
smiled confidently, doing his best to keep their
spirits high. ~~_How did the soldiers feel about Lee_~~
~~_if they cheered and waved their hats?_~~ Later that morning, though, things did
not go exactly according to Lee’s plans. The Confederate forces attacked,
hoping to break through the Union lines and send the enemy retreating from
the field. Lee knew that if he succeeded, the South would have a chance to
win the war. If he lost it may not. ~~_What do you think is going to happen?_~~


**Show Image 9A-7: Pickett’s Charge**


The battle went on all day, but the most
important moment came when Lee ordered
General Pickett to lead his men in a daring
charge across a wide, open field directly at the
middle of the Union lines. The move, known as
Pickett’s Charge, was a catastrophe for the
Confederates. ~~_A catastrophe is an event that_~~
~~_causes great trouble or destruction. This means that Pickett’s Charge caused_~~
~~_a great deal of trouble for the Confederate side._~~ Despite Pickett and his men’s
efforts, at the end of that third day, the Union still held the high ground. Lee
had lost the battle and had to retreat to Virginia, abandoning hopes of
invading deep into the North.


**Show Image 9A-8: Woman Mourning**


The day after the battle was the Fourth of July,
a day when Americans normally celebrate
their independence. ~~_From what country did_~~
~~_Americans gain independence? (Great Britain)_~~
In 1863, however, celebrations were not so
cheerful. Even in the North, where word
quickly spread that the Union had won a
major battle at Gettysburg, a war-torn nation was exhausted from battle. In
the three days of the battle at Gettysburg, many, many men had died, were
injured, or had been captured on both the Union and Confederate sides. Few
people on either side found a reason to celebrate.



Support


Have students identify
who was referred to as
“The Old Man.”

**Show Image 9A-9: Lincoln at Gettysburg**


A few months after the battle, President Lincoln
went to Gettysburg to deliver a 2-minute-long
speech. It is known as the Gettysburg Address
and, even though it is short, it is one of the
most powerful speeches in history. Lincoln’s
Gettysburg Address reminded people what the
Union was fighting for: the survival of a nation
built on liberty and equality ~~_or freedom and fairness._~~


Here’s some of what he said: “Our fathers brought forth, upon this continent,
a new nation, conceived ~~_or created_~~ in Liberty, and dedicated to the
proposition ~~_or idea_~~ that all men are created equal. Now we are engaged in ~~_or_~~
~~_in the middle of_~~ a great civil war, testing whether that nation, or any nation so
conceived, and so dedicated, can long endure ~~_or last_~~ . … [T]his nation, under
God, shall have a new birth of freedom — and that government of the people,
by the people, for the people, shall not perish ~~_or die_~~ from the earth.”


As Lincoln saw it, America’s founding principles of liberty and equality were
being put to the test. And they were worth fighting for. ~~_How do you think_~~
~~_President Lincoln’s speech might affect the outcome of the war?_~~


Check for Understanding


**Take a Side:** I am going to read several statements about the Battle of
Gettysburg. If the statement refers to the Union at the Battle of Gettysburg,
walk quietly to the front of the room. If the statement refers to the
Confederacy at the Battle of Gettysburg, walk quietly to the back of the room.


        - This side was led by General Robert E. Lee at the Battle of Gettysburg.


» the Confederacy; back of room


        - This side won the Battle of Gettysburg.


» the Union; front of room


        - The soldiers on this side affectionately called their leader

“The Old Man.”


» the Confederacy; back of room


       - This side ordered its soldiers to make a daring charge, known as

Pickett’s Charge, which turned out to be a catastrophe for them.


» (the Confederacy; back of room)



Unit 7 The U.S. Civil War
**150**


~~**COMPREHENSION QUESTIONS (10 MIN.)**~~


1. **Literal.** How did Robert E. Lee become the commander of the Confederate

Army?


» At first, he refused to join the Confederate Army, but he also refused

President Lincoln’s offer to take command of the Union Army. Because
he was from Virginia, he agreed to take command of the Confederate
Army only after that state seceded from the Union.


2. **Literal.** How did Confederate soldiers feel about General Lee?


» They loved and respected him.


3. **Literal.** Why did General Lee refuse at first to command the Confederate

Army?


» He did not agree with the Southern states seceding from the

United States.


   - Why did he change his mind?


» When his own state of Virginia seceded, he decided he would rather

fight with Virginia than against it.


4. **Inferential.** _Think-Pair-Share_ : What do you think President Lincoln meant

by “[T]his nation, under God, shall have a new birth of freedom—and that
government of the people, by the people, for the people, shall not perish from
the earth”?


» Answers may vary, but students might identify that Lincoln was

thinking about the abolishment of slavery when he says the nation will
have “a new birth of freedom,” or that he believes the end of slavery and
the war will make the government stronger so it “shall not perish from
the earth.”


5. **Evaluative.** _Think-Pair-Share:_ What does the author most likely want the

reader to learn about General Lee?


» Answers may vary but could include that his soldiers respected him, he

was a good student in school, at first he refused to lead the Confederate
or Union armies, he was proud to serve in the army, he was a powerful
and recognizable figure, etc.


6. **Inferential.** _Think-Pair-Share:_ Why do you think that at this point in the war,

“few people on either side found reason to celebrate”?


» Students will likely point out that the amount of death and destruction

affected both sides and that the war was taking longer than expected
without achieving their goals.



Speaking and Listening
Supporting Own Opinions


Beginning
During Think-Pair-Share,
students will support
their opinions about why
few people on either
side found a reason to
celebrate by providing a
reason using _because_ and
some evidence from the
Read-Aloud or relevant
background knowledge.
Student responses may
include pointing, gesturing,
and/or sketching.


Intermediate
During Think-Pair-Share,
students will support their
opinions about why few
people on either side found
a reason to celebrate by
providing a reason using
_because_ and increasingly
detailed evidence from the
Read-Aloud or relevant
background knowledge.


Advanced/
Advanced High
During Think-Pair-Share,
students will support their
opinions about why few
people on either side found
a reason to celebrate by
providing multiple reasons
and detailed evidence from
the Read-Aloud or relevant
background knowledge.

Lesson 9 Robert E. Lee
**151**


~~**WORD WORK: ADVISORS (5 MIN.)**~~


1. In the Read-Aloud, you heard, “This image shows Confederate President
Jefferson Davis and his closest advisors, including General Lee in the middle,
discussing their war plan.”


2. Say the word _advisors_ with me.


3. Advisors are people who give suggestions or advice.


4. Teachers, parents, coaches, and friends can all be advisors.


5. Who do you think of as your advisors? Have you ever been an advisor to
another person? Use the word _advisors_ or _advisor_ in a complete sentence
when you tell about it. [Ask two or three students. If necessary, guide and/or
rephrase students’ responses: “_____ were advisors to me when _____.” or “I
was an advisor once when _____.”]


6. What’s the word we’ve been talking about? What part of speech is the word
_advisors_ ?


**Use a Making Choices activity for follow-up.** I am going to read some
sentences. If I describe people giving advice, say, “_____ were advisors,” or
“_____ was an advisor.” If I do not describe people giving advice, say, “_____
were not advisors,” or “_____ was not an advisor.”


                 - General Lee helped Confederate President Jefferson Davis to make a battle
plan. _(General Lee was an advisor.)_


                  - All of the students sat at their desks in silence. _(The students were not_
_advisors.)_


                - Meredith and Gabby spoke with each other to see what the other thought
about something. _(Meredith and Gabby were advisors.)_


                  - My teacher told me I should try out for the spelling bee. _(My teacher was an_
_advisor.)_


                 - The new class president didn’t let students give her suggestions. _(Students_
_were not advisors to the new class president.)_

~~**SOMEBODY, WANTED, BUT, SO, THEN (10 MIN.)**~~


  - Display Somebody, Wanted, But, So, Then Class Chart and remind students
they have used Somebody, Wanted, But, So, Then charts before in Lesson 2.


  - Explain that students are going to use this chart to retell—first in pairs, and
then together as a class—how Robert E. Lee came to be the commander of
the Confederate Army.


  - Explain that they are going to retell Lee’s story using Activity Page 9.1. After
students complete their work with a partner, use the Somebody, Wanted,
But, So, Then Class Chart to complete the class chart as a whole group so
that it looks like the following:

|Somebody|General Robert E. Lee|
|---|---|
|Wanted|<br> <br>_to find a peaceful way to end the disagreement_<br>_between the North and the South and wanted to_<br>_keep his oath to the Constitution_|
|But|<br>_his own state of Virginia seceded from the United_<br>_States_|
|So|<br>_he decided, rather than fight against Virginia, to_<br>_command the Confederate Army_|
|Then|<br>_he used his skill to lead the Confederate Army to_<br>_several victories_|

sources in meaningful ways such as illustrating or writing.

**Turn and Talk:** Talk to your partner about Robert E. Lee, using these
questions to guide your discussion:


      - What important job did General Robert E. Lee have in the U.S. Civil War?


      - What kind of a person do you think General Robert E. Lee was?


      - Do you think he was a good general? Why or why not?


      - What was General Lee’s role at the Battle of Gettysburg?

their partner, have students write two or three sentences on Activity Page 9.2
about General Robert E. Lee and the role he played in the U.S. Civil War.


 - If time allows, students may also illustrate what they have written.


 - Give students the opportunity to share their writing and drawings with a
partner or with the class.

use an alternate U.S. map for support.


                 - Prepare to display and refer to the Global Map during the reading, or prepare
to use an alternate global map for support.

**Application**


                 - Prepare to distribute Image Cards 11 and 12 to support students’ work in the
Civil War Timeline activity.
**Universal Access**

**Introducing the Read-Aloud**


                 - Prepare and provide printed lists of the prompts before the Check for
Understanding activity to allow for visual support and increased processing
time.


**Read-Aloud**


                 - Provide sentence starters for students to access during their Think-PairShare discussions:


                        - I think “Angel of the Battlefield” was/was not an appropriate nickname for

Clara Barton because _____.


                        - I know this because in the Read-Aloud, _____.


**Application**


                 - Prepare an exemplar Civil War Journal Entry to share as a model, noting the

types of words, sentences, and details that are included.


Unit 7 The U.S. Civil War
**158**


~~**CORE VOCABULARY**~~


**aid, n.** help or assistance

Example: The doctors provided medicine and other _aid_ for the earthquake
victims.
Variation(s): aid (v.)


**chaos, n.** state of total confusion and disorder

Example: There was total _chaos_ on the beach when a shark fin appeared in
the water.
Variation(s): democratic


**compassionate, adj.** caring; having or showing sympathy or pity

Example: Kimani should be a veterinarian because she is so _compassionate_
toward animals.
Variation(s): compassion


**countless, adj.** too many to count

Example: The stars in the sky are _countless_ .
Variation(s): none


**destructive, adj.** harmful and damaging

Example: The puppy was very _destructive_ to my mother’s favorite couch.
Variation(s): destruct, destruction


**disasters, n.** events that cause a lot of destruction and pain

Example: The Red Cross quickly responds after natural _disasters_ such as
tornadoes and earthquakes have occurred.
Variation(s): disaster


**ensured, v.** made certain of

Example: Laura’s mom _ensured_ she finished her homework before she
watched TV.
Variation(s): ensure


**volunteers, n** people who donate their time for free to help other people in
need

Example: At the local soup kitchen, _volunteers_ work to feed the homeless
every day.
Variation(s): volunteer (v.)


**wounded, v.** injured or hurt

Example: After the fire, the people who were _wounded_ were transported
quickly to the hospital.
Variation(s): wound, wounds, wounding

#### Introducing the Read-Aloud



10m



**Primary Focus:** Students will review information about Robert E. Lee and the role

he played in the Civil War.


~~**TEKS 2.1.C**~~


~~**WHAT HAVE WE ALREADY LEARNED? (10 MIN.)**~~


**Show Image 9A-6: Lee Greeting His Soldiers.**


  - Ask students to identify the man in this image (Robert E. Lee).


  - Display the completed chart from the Model Somebody Wanted But So Then
chart, and invite students to access their own completed charts on Activity
Page 9.1. Have students review the included information.


Check for Understanding


**Thumbs-Up/Thumbs-Down:** I am going to read several statements.
If the statement correctly states a fact about Robert E. Lee, give a
thumbs-up signal. If the statement does not state a fact about Robert
E. Lee, give a thumbs-down signal. If you give a thumbs-down signal,
tell me what information would make the statement correct.


        - Robert E. Lee was asked by President Lincoln to lead the Union Army.

_(thumbs-up)_


        - Robert E. Lee was asked by Jefferson Davis, president of the

Confederacy, to lead the Confederate Army. _(thumbs-up)_


        - Robert E. Lee was from the state of New York. _(thumbs-down; Robert E._

_Lee was from the state of Virginia.)_


         - Robert E. Lee was affectionately called “the Old General” by his troops.

_(thumbs-down; Robert E. Lee was affectionately called “The Old Man.”)_


        - Robert E. Lee was the commander of the losing side in the Battle of

Gettysburg. _(thumbs-up)_


**TEKS 2.1.C** Share information and ideas that focus on the topic under discussion, speaking clearly at an appropriate pace
and using the conventions of language.

Lesson 10 Clara Barton

**Lesson 10: Clara Barton**
#### Read-Aloud



30m



**Reading:** Students will explain why Clara Barton became known as “the Angel of

the Battlefield.”


~~**TEKS 2.6.F; TEKS 2.6.G**~~


**Language:** Students will demonstrate an understanding of the Tier 2 word

_wounded_ .


~~**TEKS 2.3.B**~~


~~**PURPOSE FOR LISTENING**~~


  - Today’s Read-Aloud is about Clara Barton and the contributions she made in
the Civil War.


  - Tell students to listen carefully to learn what nickname Clara Barton earned
and why she got that nickname.


~~**“CLARA BARTON” (15 MIN.)**~~


**Show Image 10A-1: Clara Barton**



Flip Book Images
10A-1–10A-8



The Civil War was destructive ~~_or harmful and_~~
~~_damaging_~~ ~~.~~ More Americans died in the Civil
War than in any other war that America has
fought. ~~_More American soldiers were killed_~~
~~_and injured in the Civil War compared to the_~~

~~_more advanced and Americans were killing_~~
~~_each other. Also, the care for the injured soldiers was very poor. Listen carefully_~~
~~_to hear who will help improve the care given to injured soldiers._~~





As horrible as it is, times of war can sometimes bring out the best in people.
Some individuals choose to fight not to destroy other armies, but to save
lives. Clara Barton was one such person. She wished to reduce the suffering
and pain of others. She was a schoolteacher from Massachusetts ~~[Display~~
~~the U.S. Map, and point to Massachusetts.]~~ who had always been known as a
loving, **compassionate** person. This means that she cared for other people


**TEKS 2.6.F** Make inferences and use evidence to support understanding; **TEKS 2.6.G** Evaluate details read to determine key
ideas; **TEKS 2.3.B** Use context within and beyond a sentence to determine the meaning of unfamiliar words.


Unit 7 The U.S. Civil War
**162**


and wanted to make their lives better. ~~_What does_~~ ~~compassionate~~ ~~_mean?_~~
Clara Barton had no formal schooling as a medical nurse. By the end of the
war, however, she would become one of the most famous nurses in history.


Clara Barton was in Washington, D.C. after the First Battle of Manassas.

~~[Have a student point to Washington, D.C. on the U.S. Map.]~~ Hundreds
of **wounded** or ~~_injured_~~ Union soldiers returned there after losing a battle
that everyone thought they would win. The hospitals in the city were
overcrowded. There were not enough beds or medical supplies to care for the
injured soldiers. Clara Barton immediately went around the city collecting
bandages and medicine from people’s homes.


**Show Image 10A-2: Clara Barton Advocating**
**for Better Medical Care**



Clara Barton helped to care for and save
hundreds of wounded soldiers after the First
Battle of Manassas. During this time, she

and politicians were busy figuring out how to
build their armies and win battles. Nobody had thought seriously about how
to take care of the thousands of men who would get hurt in battle. ~~_Do you_~~
~~_think this was fair to the soldiers?_~~ So, Clara Barton decided she would do
something about it herself.





She began by writing letters and visiting doctors, politicians, and other
leaders. She encouraged them to spend more money on medical supplies for
the soldiers. She visited women’s groups, churches, and hospitals. She called
on wealthy individuals to donate ~~_or give_~~ medical supplies and money. Soon,
Clara Barton had collected a large assortment of supplies, but the supplies
needed to be delivered to the battlefield to be of any use. So, she continued
to look for solutions. ~~_What do you think Clara Barton is going to do?_~~


**Show Image 10A-3: Injured Soldiers**


Those who were wounded in battle
experienced terrible suffering. ~~_Look at this_~~
~~_picture. Who in this image were wounded?_~~
They were often left lying on the field for an

come and carry them away. Field hospitals
are where the wounded were taken during and after battles. They were
sometimes set up in nearby barns or houses. Sometimes, they were set up in
a group of tattered tents.





Lesson 10 Clara Barton
**163**


Soldiers in overcrowded field hospitals often found themselves alone. They
were hurt with nobody to bring them food or water. They had nobody to
comfort them and ease their pain. The doctors were simply too busy and too
tired to help everyone. Thousands of men died. They could have lived if the
hospitals had the supplies they needed.


**Show Image 10A-4: Barton Following Army**
**with Her Supplies**





Clara Barton started following the main Union
Army wherever it went. This army protected
Washington, D.C. Its ultimate goal was to
attack Richmond, the Confederate capital,
and win the war. ~~_In which state is Richmond_~~
~~_located?_~~



Challenge


Have students explain
why capturing an army’s
capital would help that
side win a war.



She took wagon loads of bandages and other supplies to field hospitals. Clara
Barton also **ensured** the doctors had what they needed. She made food
for the sick and wounded whenever possible. She also brought them water
and blankets. Clara Barton comforted them and wiped the sweat from their
foreheads. Many times she fixed their bandages and simply talked to them.


Clara Barton was determined to do even more. She wanted to be able to help
soldiers on the battlefield, who often had to wait a long time to be moved
to a hospital. Unfortunately, women were not allowed on the battlefields. At
least, that is what the generals told her whenever she asked to help during
the battles. ~~_Why do you think women were not allowed on the battlefields?_~~
But Clara Barton kept asking and insisting. Finally, in 1862, she received
permission to go to the heart of the battles.


**Show Image 10A-5: Clara Barton Caring for**
**Wounded on Battlefield**


Clara Barton became known as the “Angel of
the Battlefield.” In the middle of the **chaos** of
war, soldiers and doctors were always glad to
see her calm face. ~~_What does_~~ ~~chaos~~ ~~_mean?_~~ At
the Battle of Antietam, more than 12,000 Union
soldiers were wounded. This was far more than
she and the other nurses and doctors could care for. But they did their best.
Once a battle was over, she would hurry back to Washington, D.C. Clara Barton
would collect more supplies and then catch up with the army again.





Unit 7 The U.S. Civil War
**164**


**Show Image 10A-6: Army Ambulances**



By the middle of 1863, the Union Army figured
out how to make sure the field hospitals
had enough supplies. This was partly thanks
to Clara Barton. She kept pressure on ~~_or_~~
~~_continued to ask for help from_~~ the War

D.C., to make real changes. She no longer had
to collect supplies, but she continued to follow the army for the remainder of
the war. She acted as the “Angel of the Battlefield” to **countless** —more than
can be counted—wounded soldiers.





Clara Barton saw a lot of bloodshed and fighting. She was at some of the
worst battles. She worked as bullets and cannonballs whistled overhead and
crashed all around. Once, a bullet tore right through her shirt sleeve. But she
was very brave. She did not let fear stop her from doing what she needed to
do. ~~_How do you think Clara felt during those times?_~~


**Show Image 10A-7: Barton Overseas**


When the war ended, Clara Barton continued
to find ways to help others. In fact, she was
only just beginning. She went to Europe and
worked as a nurse in wars there. ~~[Display~~
~~the Global Map, and point to the continent of~~

~~the map as they are mentioned.]~~ During her
life, she worked in Turkey, China, Cuba, and other countries. She returned to
America and, in 1881, started the American Red Cross.



Support


Review the meaning of
the word _countless._





The American Red Cross provides medical supplies, food, and other **aid** ~~_or_~~
~~_help_~~ during natural **disasters**, such as floods and earthquakes.


**Show Image 10A-8: Red Cross Today**


Today, the American Red Cross is still run by
**volunteers** . These are people who donate
their time for free to help other people in need.
Clara Barton helped countless people during
her lifetime.





There are still wars and other disasters in
this world. Clara Barton would be glad to know that the American Red Cross
continues to save lives and give comfort to people in need to this very day.

Supporting Own Opinions


Beginning
During Think-Pair-Share,
students will support their
opinions about whether or not

“the Angel of the Battlefield”
was an appropriate nickname

for Clara Barton by providing

a reason using _because_
and some evidence from
the Read-Aloud or relevant

background knowledge.
Student responses may
include pointing, gesturing,

and/or sketching.


Intermediate
During Think-Pair-Share,
students will support their
opinions about whether or not

“the Angel of the Battlefield”
was an appropriate nickname

for Clara Barton by providing

a reason using _because_
and increasingly detailed
evidence from the Read-Aloud

or relevant background

knowledge.


Advanced/Advanced High

Students will support their
opinions about whether or not

“the Angel of the Battlefield”
was an appropriate nickname

for Clara Barton by providing
multiple reasons and detailed
evidence from the Read-Aloud

or relevant background

knowledge.


~~**ELPS 3.G**~~



~~**COMPREHENSION QUESTIONS (10 MIN.)**~~


If students have difficulty responding to questions, reread pertinent
passages of the Read-Aloud and/or refer to specific images. If students
give one-word answers and/or fail to use Read-Aloud or unit vocabulary in
their responses, acknowledge correct responses by expanding students’
responses using richer and more complex language. Ask students to answer in
complete sentences by having them restate the question in their responses.


1. **Inferential.** How did Clara Barton feel about the soldiers?


» She felt it was very important to provide better medical care to the

soldiers.


   - What information in the Read-Aloud lets you know how she felt?


» She worked hard to gather the supplies she needed, and she followed

the army to many of the battles, where she risked her own life to
provide medical care to the soldiers.


2. **Literal.** What is the name of the organization Clara Barton founded?


» the American Red Cross


   - Is this organization still in existence today?


» Yes


   - What does the Red Cross do today?


» It helps people during times of war or other disasters.


3. **Inferential.** Which happened first: the start of the Civil War, or the start of
the American Red Cross?


» The start of the Civil War


4. **Evaluative.** _Think-Pair-Share:_ Do you think “the Angel of the Battlefield”
was an appropriate nickname for Clara Barton? Be sure to provide evidence
from the Read-Aloud to support your answer.


» Answers may vary but should reflect information in the text, including

the fact that she was helpful to people who were injured in battle and
she did much of her work on the battlefields, even while bullets and
cannonballs continued to fly during the battle.



Unit 7 The U.S. Civil War
**166**


Check for Understanding


**Recall:** What was the nickname Clara Barton earned during the Civil
War? _(the Angel of the Battlefield)_ How did she earn this nickname?
_(She worked hard to obtain medical supplies needed to treat the soldiers’_
_wounds, and then she delivered the supplies and helped care for the_
_soldiers on the battlefields, risking her own safety.)_


~~**WORD WORK: WOUNDED (5 MIN.)**~~


1. In the Read-Aloud you heard, “At the Battle of Antietam, more than 12,000
Union soldiers were wounded.”


2. Say the word _wounded_ with me.


3. _Wounded_ means to be injured or hurt.


4. The Red Cross helped care for the people who were _wounded_ by the tornado.


5. Who else might help people who are wounded? [Ask two or three students.
If necessary, guide and/or rephrase students’ responses: “_____ also help
people who are wounded.”]


6. What’s the word we’ve been talking about?


**Use a Making Choices activity for follow-up.** You have heard that if
someone is wounded it means that they have been hurt or injured. I am going
to read several sentences. If the person or animal has been hurt or injured,
say, “_____ was/were wounded.” If the person or animal is fine, say, “_____
was/were not wounded.”


  - Many soldiers were injured during the war.


» Many soldiers were wounded.


  - Molly tripped but did not get hurt.


» Molly was not wounded.


  - The puppy jumped off the bed and hurt its paw.


» The puppy was wounded.


  - Katya fell off the swing and needed a bandage.

  - Amos felt wonderful when he ate his birthday cupcake.


» Amos was not wounded.

  - Tell students they will add to the Civil War Timeline they started in an earlier
lesson.


  - Review the events that have already been depicted on the timeline.


**Show Image Card 11 (Clara Barton)**


  - Have students describe the important work Clara Barton did during the Civil
War.


  - Have a student place the image card on the timeline to show when Clara
Barton helped soldiers on the battlefield. _(to the right of the formation of the_
_Confederacy)_


**Show Image Card 12 (Symbol for Red Cross)**


  - Ask students if Clara Barton founded the American Red Cross before or after
she helped soldiers during the Civil War. _(after)_


  - Have a student place the image card on the timeline to show that Clara
Barton founded the American Red Cross after the Civil War.


  - Save the timeline for future lessons.

~~**CIVIL WAR JOURNAL (15 MIN)**~~


 - Tell students they will write another entry for the Civil War journal they began

 - Explain that students will identify Clara Barton and describe her
accomplishments both during and after the Civil War.


Check for Understanding


**Adjective Action:** What are some adjectives the author of the ReadAloud uses to describe Clara Barton? _(compassionate, determined, calm,_
_brave)_ What adjectives would you add to describe Clara Barton? _(Answers_
_may vary, but students might identify descriptors such as smart, kind,_
_resourceful, caring, or helpful.)_


 - Have students use the information heard in the Read-Aloud, and the
adjectives they discussed, to write two or three sentences identifying Clara
Barton and describing her accomplishments.


 - If time allows, students may also illustrate what they have written.


 - Give students the opportunity to share their writing and drawings with a
partner or with the class.

Lesson 11 Ulysses S. Grant
**171**


~~**ADVANCE PREPARATION**~~


**Read-Aloud**


                 - Prepare to display the U.S. Map. This map will be displayed throughout the

lesson.


**Application**


                 - Prepare to display and refer to Poster 2M: Post during the Multiple-Meaning

Word activity.


**Universal Access**

**Introducing the Read-Aloud**


                 - Prepare and provide a list of the prompts during the Check for

Understanding activity.


**Read-Aloud**


                 - Prepare and provide a Venn Diagram or another graphic organizer during the

Check for Understanding activity to support a comparison of the Union and

Confederate armies.


**Application**


                  - Provide students with a list of prompts to guide their illustrations or written
responses in the Civil War Journal activity (e.g., How can you describe/show
the differences between General Lee and General Grant in your writing/
illustration? How can you show their similarities? How could you show their
leadership roles? What important details from the Read-Aloud could you
show in your illustration or writing?)


                 - Prepare and provide a set of example sentences using _post_ differently to
reinforce student understanding of the word’s multiple meanings.


~~**CORE VOCABULARY**~~


**ammunition, n.** material fired from weapons such as guns and cannons
Example: The soldier carefully loaded the _ammunition_ in the cannon.
Variation(s): none


**defeat, n.** failure to win

Example: Len’s soccer team experienced a disappointing _defeat_ when the
opposing team scored three goals and his team scored none.
Variation(s): defeats, defeat (v.)


**rations, n.** amounts of food or provisions set aside for each person


Unit 7 The U.S. Civil War
**172**


Example: There were just enough _rations_ in the space station for three
astronauts.
Variation(s): ration


**Yankees, n.** Union soldiers during the Civil War; people from the Northern

States
Example: During the Civil War, the _Yankees_ were fighting against the Rebels.
Variation(s): Yankee

~~**ELPS 2.G; ELPS 3.F**~~



**Speaking and Listening:** Students will review information about Clara Barton and

her accomplishments.


~~**TEKS 2.1.C**~~


~~**WHAT HAVE WE ALREADY LEARNED? (10 MIN.)**~~


**Show Image 10A-5: Clara Barton Caring for Wounded on Battlefield**


  - Have students identify the woman in the image.


Check for Understanding


**Recall:** Prompt discussion about Clara Barton with the following
questions:


        - How did Clara Barton help the wounded during the Civil War?


» She obtained medical supplies to help the wounded soldiers, and
she treated the wounded on the battlefields.


        - What name was Clara Barton given and why?


» She was called the Angel of the Battlefield because she helped
the wounded soldiers.


        - How would you describe Clara Barton?


» Answers may vary but should be supported by the text and may
include brave, caring, and determined.


        - What important thing did Clara Barton do after the Civil War that we
still see the effects of today?


» She founded the American Red Cross.


**TEKS 2.1.C** Share information and ideas that focus on the topic under discussion, speaking clearly at an appropriate pace
and using the conventions of language.



Unit 7 The U.S. Civil War
**174**


**Lesson 11: Ulysses S. Grant**
30m
#### Read-Aloud


**Reading:** Students will compare and contrast the Union and Confederate

armies.

~~**TEKS 2.6.G; TEKS 2.7.B; TEKS 2.7.C**~~

**Language:** Students will demonstrate an understanding of the Tier 2 word

_defeat_ .

~~**TEKS 2.3.B; TEKS 2.3.D**~~


~~**PURPOSE FOR LISTENING**~~


  - Explain that this Read-Aloud is about a commander of the Union Army
named Ulysses S. Grant.


  - Tell students to listen carefully to learn more about Ulysses S. Grant and to
hear how he was like General Lee and how he was different from General Lee.


~~**“ULYSSES S. GRANT” (15 MIN.)**~~


**Show Image 11A-1: Ulysses S. Grant and**
**Camp**



The date was May 4, 1864. The day before,
marching with a strength of over 118,000
soldiers, the Army of the Potomac crossed the
Rapidan River in the middle of Virginia. ~~[Display~~

Ridge Mountains lay to the west. To the east lay
miles of dark forests and the Confederate Army under the command of Robert
E. Lee. General Lee had roughly 60,000 men under his command, half as many
as the Union Army, but they were ready to put up a strong fight.



Flip Book Images
11A-1–11A-8


Challenge


Have students calculate
how many soldiers were
in the Union Army based
on the fact that there
were 60,000 men in the
Confederate Army and
the Read-Aloud said that
was half as many as the
Union Army.





The Union Army was commanded by Ulysses S. Grant. ~~[Point to Grant in the~~
~~image.]~~ He was no stranger to battle. He had served in the army for over 25
years, starting when he was just 17 years old. ~~_This was just like Robert E. Lee._~~
The Civil War was not his first war, either. Like Confederate General Robert E.
Lee, General Grant had fought in another war.


**TEKS 2.6.G** Evaluate details read to determine key ideas; **TEKS 2.7.B** Write brief comments on literary or informational texts

Lesson 11 Ulysses S. Grant
**175**


Support


Explain the roles of
Ulysses S. Grant and
Robert E. Lee as leaders
of the Union and
Confederate armies
to the students. Help
them understand how
their battle experiences
shaped their leadership.



General Ulysses S. Grant leaned against a post outside his tent. ~~_The word_~~
~~post~~ ~~_in this sentence means a piece of wood or metal that is set into the_~~
~~_ground in an upright position._~~


He wearily ~~_or with tiredness_~~ watched as a long line of supply wagons carrying
ammunition, food, and medical supplies rumbled past. ~~_The word_~~ ~~ammunition~~
~~_refers to the bullets, cannonballs, etc. that are shot out of weapons._~~ These supply
wagons made up the rear of the army. The main body of the army, the soldiers
who needed all those supplies in order to fight, were miles ahead, deep in the
forest, looking for the enemy. ~~_Who was the enemy of the Union Army?_~~


**Show Image 11A-2: Lincoln Gives Grant**
**Orders**


General Grant was now the general in charge
of the entire Union Army. The only person
who ranked higher than General Grant was
President Abraham Lincoln. ~~[Point out Lincoln~~

from Lincoln, and everyone else took their
orders from Grant. ~~_What title does the president have as the highest-ranking_~~
~~_commander? (commander in chief)_~~ Even though the President was in charge
and had the final say, Lincoln and Grant worked well together, trusted each
other, and grew to greatly respect one another.





They also had a lot in common. Both were very dedicated to their families,
they had strong moral character, they didn’t curse, they didn’t care about
appearances, and they loved animals. They also had similar experiences
as kids growing up in the Midwest. ~~[Display the U.S. Map, and point to the~~
~~Midwest region, highlighting Lincoln’s home state of Illinois and Grant’s~~
~~home state of Ohio.]~~ But what really made them alike was their mutual
understanding that war was dangerous and hard.


All throughout the Civil War, Lincoln and Grant were willing to do whatever it
took to win, and they were not going to give up.


Unit 7 The U.S. Civil War
**176**


**Show Image 11A-3: Grant Out West**


Every general in the war faced hard choices
and had heavy responsibilities, with the lives
of thousands of soldiers in his hands. But
in 1864, no general had more worries than
General Grant. ~~_Why do you think General Grant_~~
~~_had so many worries?_~~



General Grant had spent the first three years of the Civil War fighting farther
west, away from the action in Virginia. His most impressive victory in the
early years of the war came at Vicksburg, a city in Mississippi. ~~[Display and~~
~~point to Mississippi on the U.S. Map. Point to the Mississippi River as you~~
~~mention it.]~~


The same day that the Union Army had won the Battle of Gettysburg,
General Grant won the Battle of Vicksburg, after two long, hard months. The
victory gave the Union final control over the entire Mississippi River, which
in turn would make it easier for the Union to take over the rest of the South.
The Mississippi River was important because the Union could use it to send
troops and supplies from the North to the South. It was easier to use a river
to do this because there were no cars or trucks yet, and so there were no
highways like we have today.


**Show Image 11A-4: Well-Supplied**
**Northern Army/Ragged Southern Army**



Challenge


Have students think back
to what they learned in
Unit 4, _The War of 1812_ .
Ask them to describe
the importance of the
Mississippi River during
the War of 1812. (The river
was one of the targets of
the British, who helped to
control the waterways and
the Americans’ resupply
routes.)





To win the Civil War, the Union needed to take
control of the South, including all of its cities
and roads. In the beginning, nobody in the
North expected this to be so difficult.



Factories in the North had been working day
and night for years, producing weapons, uniforms, blankets, food **rations**,
wagons, and all of the other things the army needed. ~~Rations~~ ~~_are amounts_~~
~~_of food and other materials set aside for each person. Was all this production_~~
~~_from factories good for the Northern economy?_~~ The **Yankees**, as the Union
soldiers were nicknamed, had everything they needed to fight and win the
war. What was the nickname for the Union soldiers? ~~_What was the nickname_~~
~~_for Confederate soldiers? (Rebels) Why do you think the North expected to_~~
~~_win so easily?_~~


Lesson 11 Ulysses S. Grant
**177**


The Confederates, or Rebels as they were often called, did not have as many
men as the Union. The South did not have many factories; many of those it
did have were destroyed or captured by 1864. Confederate soldiers marched
to battle without shoes, without enough food, and sometimes without
enough ammunition. ~~_What is ammunition?_~~ Yet, even though they were
exhausted and starved, the Confederates somehow held on and managed to
keep fighting.


**Show Image 11A-5: General Grant**



Grant was not the general in chief of the Union
Army ~~_or commander of all of the U.S. armies_~~
at the beginning of the Civil War. Throughout
the war, President Lincoln had trouble with
some of his top Union generals. It wasn’t that
they were bad generals; they could win battles
and capture enemy forts and towns. But
they made mistakes, as well. They often waited too long to attack or failed
to chase the Confederates when they were on the run. Basically, President
Lincoln felt the Union generals were never aggressive, or forceful, enough.
Also, they were quick to blame President Lincoln when they lost battles,
rather than take responsibility for their failures.





But Grant was different. General Grant won the long Battle of Vicksburg
because he was stubborn and fearless; he kept fighting and attacking until
the enemy surrendered _or gave up._ ~~_What do you think_~~ ~~stubborn~~ ~~_means?_~~
President Lincoln put General Grant in charge of the entire Union Army
because General Grant promised that he would do whatever it took to
win; he would chase General Robert E. Lee and his army all over Virginia,
and he would not stop until the war was finished. He earned the nickname
“Unconditional Surrender” because he would accept nothing less from the
Confederate Army than a complete surrender. ~~_Do you think General Grant_~~
~~_will be able to get the Confederate Army to completely surrender?_~~


Unit 7 The U.S. Civil War
**178**


**Show Image 11A-6: Grant Reading Letter**
**from Lincoln**


President Lincoln sent a letter to General Grant.
It did not have any important information or
new orders. It was just a simple letter sent to
wish him good luck in battle. The letter was
written in the president’s handwriting:



_Lieutenant-General Grant—_


_Not expecting to see you again before you march into Virginia, I wish to tell_
_you that I am entirely satisfied with what you have done up to this time . . . You_
_are alert and self-reliant; and, pleased with this, I do not wish to control your_
_actions in any way . . . If there is anything wanting which is within my power to_
_give, do not fail to let me know it._


_And now with a brave Army, and a just cause, may God sustain you_ .


_Yours very truly,_


_A. LINCOLN_


~~_[Re-read portions to support comprehension. “I am entirely satisfied” – I am_~~
~~_happy with your performance. “If there is anything wanting” – If you need_~~
~~_anything. “a just cause” – we are fighting to ensure freedom for our fellow_~~
~~_Americans, and it is the right thing to do.]_~~


**Show Image 11A-7: Battle of the**
**Wilderness**



Challenge


Invite students to work
with a partner to define
alert and self-reliant using
the context of the reading
and their prior knowledge.


Support


Review the definition of
the word _clash_, which
students learned in an
earlier lesson.





The next day, May 5, in the forests near
Fredericksburg, Virginia, Grant’s army clashed
with General Lee’s army in one of the most
chaotic battles of the war. ~~[Point to Virginia on~~
~~the U.S. Map.]~~



In those days, armies always preferred to fight in open fields, where it was
easier to move cannons and large groups of men, and easier for generals
to see what was happening. This time, though, the armies met deep in the
woods, where the tree and plant growth were so heavy that the soldiers
could barely see one another.


Lesson 11 Ulysses S. Grant
**179**


Challenge


Have students define the

word _chaotic_ based on
the way it is used in this

paragraph.



This was called the Battle of the Wilderness, and it was the very first time
Generals Grant and Lee faced each other in battle. It was a very chaotic
battle. Thousands were killed and wounded. At the end of the day, both
armies limped away ~~_or left with difficulty because of their injuries_~~, with no
clear winner in the battle.


**Show Image 11A-8: Clara Barton Tending**
**Wounded**



After the battle, many of the Union wounded
were taken to churches and homes in the
nearby city of Fredericksburg. Clara Barton

to wounded soldiers. ~~_Who was Clara Barton?_~~
~~_What was her nickname?_~~ The next day,
hundreds more wounded soldiers were brought in from yet another battle.
And on it went.





The armies of Grant and Lee met again and again during the months that
followed. Sometimes Grant won the battle, sometimes Lee won, and sometimes
nobody won. But with each battle, the Confederate Army got a little smaller and
that much closer to final **defeat.** ~~_The word_~~ ~~defeat~~ ~~_means a failure to win. Does_~~
~~_this last sentence give you a clue about who will win the war?_~~


Unit 7 The U.S. Civil War
**180**


~~**COMPREHENSION QUESTIONS (10 MIN.)**~~


1. **Literal.** [Show Image 11A-5: General Grant] Who is pictured in this image?


» Ulysses S. Grant


2. **Literal.** What important job did Ulysses S. Grant have during the Civil War?


» He was general in chief or commander of the Union Army.


3. **Inferential.** Why did President Lincoln ask him to take over the command of
the Union Army?


» He had a reputation for doing whatever it took to win, and the earlier
commanders were not winning the war.


4. **Literal.** Was Grant the commander at the beginning of the Civil War?


» No


5. **Literal.** Why was Grant given the nickname Unconditional Surrender?


» He accepted nothing less than a complete surrender.


6. **Evaluative.** In the Read-Aloud, you heard that General Grant won the Battle
of Vicksburg because he was stubborn and unafraid. How might being
stubborn and unafraid help someone win a battle in a war?


» Answers may vary, but students may identify that these qualities could

make sure someone was so committed to winning the battle that they
would not back down, no matter how dangerous or scary.


7. **Literal.** What nickname was given to Union soldiers?


» Yankees


8. **Literal.** What nickname was given to the Confederate soldiers?


» Rebels



Support


Before asking the
comprehension questions,
review the relevant parts of
the text and summarize key
points to ensure students
have a good understanding
of the material.


Flip Book 11A-5



Lesson 11 Ulysses S. Grant
**181**


**EMERGENT**
**BILINGUAL**
**STUDENTS**


Speaking and Listening
Supporting Own Opinions


Beginning
During Think-Pair-Share,
students will support their
opinions about whether the
differences between the
armies eventually led to the
defeat of the Confederate
Army by providing a
reason using _because_ and
some evidence from the
Read-Aloud or relevant
background knowledge.
Student responses may
include pointing, gesturing,
and/or sketching.


Intermediate
During Think-Pair-Share,
students will support their

opinions about whether
the differences between

the armies eventually
led to the defeat of the

Confederate Army by
providing a reason using
_because_ and increasingly
detailed evidence from the

Read-Aloud or relevant
background knowledge.


Advanced/Advanced High

During Think-Pair-Share,
students will support their
opinions about whether
the differences between
the armies eventually
led to the defeat of the
Confederate army by
providing multiple reasons
and detailed evidence
from the Read-Aloud
or relevant background
knowledge.

~~**ELPS 3.G**~~



Check for Understanding


**With a Partner:** On a piece of paper, take turns with your partner writing
the ways the Confederate Army (or Rebels) was similar to the Union Army
(or the Yankees). Then, take turns writing the ways the Confederate Army
was different from the Union Army.


[Have several students share responses with the class.]


» Answers may vary but may include for similarities that they were

both intent on winning and that they were both led by strong

leaders. Answers for differences may include that the Union Army

had more soldiers, ammunition, food, and supplies. The Union

also had factories to produce supplies for the Union Army. The

Confederate Army’s soldiers marched to battle without shoes,

without enough food, and sometimes without enough ammunition.


**Evaluative** . _Think-Pair-Share_ : Do you think these differences eventually
led to the defeat of the Confederate Army? How do you know?


» Answers may vary but should reflect information in the text,

including the fact that an army that has better supplies, such as

ammunition and food, can survive battles better, and that factories

could produce the things an army needs, such as weapons,

uniforms, blankets, and wagons.



Unit 7 The U.S. Civil War
**182**


~~**WORD WORK: DEFEAT (5 MIN.)**~~


1. In the Read-Aloud you heard, “With each battle, the Confederate Army got a

little smaller and that much closer to final defeat.”


2. Say the word _defeat_ with me.


3. A defeat is a failure to win.


4. Brian scored the final point that caused the other team’s _defeat_ .


5. Have you ever experienced a loss, or defeat, or have you read about, heard
about, or seen a defeat in a movie or television show? Try to use the word
defeat when you tell about it. [Ask two or three students. If necessary, guide
and/or rephrase students’ responses: “I experienced a defeat when _____.”]


6. What’s the word we’ve been talking about?


**Use an Antonyms activity for follow-up.** You heard that a defeat is a
failure to win. The word win is an antonym, or opposite, of the word defeat.
To win means to be successful at something. I am going to read several
sentences. If I describe something that is a failure to win, say, “That is a
defeat.” If I describe something that is successful, say, “That is a win,” and
clap your hands.


 - Will beat his opponent at checkers. ( _That is a win._ )


 - Lilly missed making the goal for her soccer team. ( _That is a defeat._ )


 - Janet made a basket at the very last minute, leading her team to victory.
( _That is a win._ )


 - Robert had the lowest score in the video game against his sister. ( _That is_
_a defeat._ )


 - Patrick ranked highest at the spelling bee. ( _That is a win._ )

**Lesson 11: Ulysses S. Grant**
20m
#### Application


**Writing:** Students will write a Civil War journal entry in which they compare and

contrast Ulysses S. Grant and Robert E. Lee.


~~**TEKS 2.7.B; TEKS 2.7.C; TEKS 2.7.E**~~


~~**CIVIL WAR JOURNAL (15 MIN.)**~~


**Show Image 11A-6: Grant Reading Letter from Lincoln**


  - Tell students they will write another entry for the Civil War journal using
Activity Page 11.1.


    - Prompt further discussion about General Grant with the following
questions:


    - What kind of a person was General Grant?


    - What traits did General Grant have that made him a good general?


    - Explain that students will write one sentence describing Ulysses S. Grant
and then two or three sentences comparing and contrasting General Grant
with General Lee.


Check for Understanding


**Take a Side:** I am going to read several statements. If the statement
describes General Grant, walk quietly to the front of the room. If the
statement describes General Lee, walk quietly to the back of the room. If
the statement describes both General Lee and General Grant, stay in the
middle of the room.


        - I commanded the Union Army. _(General Grant; front of room)_


        - I commanded the Confederate Army. _(General Lee; back of room)_


        - President Lincoln asked me to lead the Union Army. _(Both General Lee_
_and General Grant; stay in middle)_


**TEKS 2.7.B** Write brief comments on literary or informational texts that demonstrate an understanding of the text; **TEKS**
**2.7.C** Use text evidence to support an appropriate response; **TEKS 2.7.E** Interact with sources in meaningful ways such as
illustrating or writing.



Unit 7 The U.S. Civil War
**184**


        - The Civil War was not the first war I fought in. _(Both General Lee and_
_General Grant; stay in middle)_


        - I spent the first few years of the Civil War fighting in the West, away
from the battles in Virginia. _(General Grant; front of room)_


        - I earned the nickname Unconditional Surrender during the Civil War.
_(General Grant; front of room)_


~~**MULTIPLE-MEANING WORD ACTIVITY: POST (5 MIN.)**~~


**Show Poster 2M (Post)**


  - Tell students they will hold up one, two, three, or four fingers to indicate
which image shows the meaning of the word being discussed.


  - Remind students that they heard in the Read-Aloud, “General Ulysses S.
Grant leaned against a _post_ outside his tent.” Ask which picture matches this
description of _post_ . (one)


  - Explain that _post_ can also mean other things, like to send something by mail,
as in to _post_ a letter. Ask which picture matches this description of _post_ .
(two)


  - Explain that _post_ can also mean to put up a sign so that it can be seen by
many people, such as when landowners _post_ “No Trespassing” signs. Ask
which picture matches this description of _post_ . (three)


  - Explain that _post_ has also developed a new meaning along with technology:
to _post_ to social media, or publicly display words or images/videos on
the Internet, so that they can be seen by many people. Ask which picture
matches this description of _post_ . (four)


  - Have students work with a partner to quiz each other on the different
meanings of the word _post_ . Remind them to be as descriptive as possible and
use complete sentences.


**End Lesson**

**EMERGENT**
**BILINGUAL**
**STUDENTS**


Writing
Comparing and Contrasting


Beginning
Allow students to dictate
or sketch to compare and
contrast Ulysses S. Grant and
Robert E. Lee with a peer or
adult. Encourage students to
label their sketches with words
and phrases in English and/
or a home language. Provide
a bank of comparing words
and phrases for students
to reference (e.g., same,
different).


Intermediate
Allow students to collaborate
with a peer to share ideas that
compare and contrast Ulysses
S. Grant and Robert E. Lee and
write their sentences. Provide
specific sentence frames (e.g.,
Both Ulysses S. Grant and
Robert E. Lee ____. Ulysses S.
Grant ____, but Robert E. Lee
____.).


Advanced/Advanced High
Challenge students to work
independently to write
their information and offer
them one-on-one feedback
specifically on language use.

could say, ‘Because it was
dark, I accidentally ran
into the fence post. Which
meaning of _post_ am I using?’
And your partner should
respond, ‘That’s one.’” **185**

### The End of Slavery in the United States


~~**PRIMARY FOCUS OF LESSON**~~

Students will summarize key facts about the Civil War.


~~**TEKS 2.7.B**~~

Students will synthesize their understandings of the costs and outcomes of the

Civil War.


~~**TEKS 2.6.G; TEKS 2.6.H**~~


**Language**

Students will demonstrate an understanding of the Tier 2 word _amendment._


~~**TEKS 2.3.D**~~


**Writing**

Students will write an entry in a Civil War journal explaining Abraham Lincoln’s

role in ending slavery in the United States.

~~**TEKS 2.7.B; TEKS 2.7.C; TEKS 2.7.E; TEKS 2.11.E**~~


~~**FORMATIVE ASSESSMENT**~~


Activity Page 12.2 **Civil War Journal: Entry 8** Write a Civil War journal
entry explaining Abraham Lincoln’s role in ending
slavery in the United States.

~~**TEKS 2.7.B; TEKS 2.7.C; TEKS 2.7.E; TEKS 2.11.E**~~


**TEKS 2.7.B** Write brief comments on literary or informational texts that demonstrate an understanding of the text; **TEKS**
**2.6.G** Evaluate details read to determine key ideas; **TEKS 2.6.H** Synthesize information to create new understanding; **TEKS**

writing; **TEKS 2.11.E** Publish and share writing.

Lesson 12 The End of Slavery in the United States
**187**


~~**ADVANCE PREPARATION**~~


**Introducing the Read-Aloud**


                - On a board/chart paper, prepare a Brainstorming Web by drawing a large

circle with the words _“The U.S. Civil War”_ in the center.


                 - Prepare student groupings for the Check for Understanding activity.


**Read-Aloud**


                 - Prepare to display and refer to the U.S. Map during the reading, or prepare to

use an alternate U.S. map for support.


**Application**


                  - Prepare to display and refer to “The Map of the Civil War.”


                  - Prepare student pairings for the Map of the Civil War activity.


                 - Prepare to distribute Image Card 13, Lee’s Surrender to Grant, to support
students’ work in the Civil War Timeline activity.


**Universal Access**

**Introducing the Read-Aloud**


                 - Consider providing students with a list of topics, events, and people from

throughout the unit to support them as they write facts about the Civil War

during the Check for Understanding activity (e.g., slavery, Harriet Tubman,

abolitionists, Abraham Lincoln, the Emancipation Proclamation, Robert E.

Lee, the Battle of Gettysburg, Clara Barton, Ulysses S. Grant).


**Read-Aloud**


                 - Provide sentence starters for students to access during the Check for

Understanding activity.


                        - I think the most important cost of the Civil War was _____. I think this
because _____.


                        - I think the most important outcome of the Civil War was _____. I think this

because _____.


**Application**


                 - Consider strategically pairing students according to their language

proficiency during the Map of the Civil War activity.


Unit 7 The U.S. Civil War

~~**CORE VOCABULARY**~~


**amendment, n.** a change or an update to something that has already been
established, usually an official document

Example: The First _Amendment_ to the U.S. Constitution provides freedom
of religion.
Variation(s): amend, amendments


**elimination, n.** removing or destroying something

Example: The _elimination_ of recess at school made all the students angry.
Variation(s): eliminate, eliminations


**permanent, adj.** long-lasting

Example: Kara’s grandfather built the garden wall out of stone so it would
be _permanent_ .
Variation(s): permanence, permanently


**ratified, v.** accepted or approved in an official way

Example: Congress _ratified_ the Bill of Rights to make sure all Americans had
basic freedoms and rights.
Variation(s): ratify, ratification


**temporary, adj.** short-term; lasting only a limited time

Example: Omar felt better when his teacher told him the seating chart was
_temporary_ .
Variation(s): temporarily

~~**“THE END OF SLAVERY IN THE UNITED STATES” (10 MIN.)**~~


**Show Image 12A-1: U.S. Capitol**


After years of fighting, the Civil War
was nearing an end. The Emancipation
Proclamation in 1863 brought the United
States one step closer to ending slavery.



Emancipation Proclamation would still be in
effect after the war ended. Lincoln knew that the Emancipation Proclamation
was only a **temporary** ~~_or short-term_~~ solution. A **permanent** ~~_or long-lasting_~~
solution was needed to end slavery in America.



Flip Book Images
12A-1–12A-7


Support


Explain the three
branches of government
and the Constitutional
idea of checks and
balances to support
student understanding
of why the Emancipation
Proclamation was only a
temporary solution until
Congress voted for the end
of slavery.





America has three branches of government. In simple terms, these branches
include the president, the lawmakers, and the judges. Each branch has certain jobs and responsibilities, and no individual branch can have more power
than the others. So, even though he was the president, Lincoln had done
all he could. The president is not a king. ~~_Why did the Founding Fathers think_~~

Lesson 12 The End of Slavery in the United States
**191**


~~_it was important to create a system of government where one person_~~ ~~(the~~
~~president)~~ ~~_doesn’t have all the power?_~~ ~~(They fought the Revolutionary War to~~
~~establish a new type of government.)~~ The president only has certain powers
given to him or her by the American people; these powers are outlined ~~_or_~~
~~_explained_~~ in the Constitution. The responsibility to find a permanent solution
fell to the lawmakers in Congress.


**Show Image 12A-2: U.S. Constitution**


An **amendment** is a change or an update to
the U.S. Constitution. The amendment that
would end slavery in the United States was
the 13th Amendment. But a lot of people in
Congress had to agree on it first. For the 13th

most of the lawmakers in Congress would have
to vote for it. Once that happened, it would have to be **ratified** (or accepted)
by the states.





The language of the 13th Amendment had been debated many times during
the Civil War. Yet even after many debates and discussions, the members
of Congress couldn’t reach an agreement. ~~_Why do you think reaching an_~~
~~_agreement on the 13th_~~ ~~Amendment~~ ~~_was so difficult?_~~


There was a real possibility that the **elimination** ~~_or removal_~~ of slavery would
not happen, even though thousands had given their lives fighting for this
cause. But something changed when Abraham Lincoln was elected president
for the second time in 1864. Lincoln’s re-election sent a clear message
that the American people wanted slavery to go away. ~~_Why did re-electing_~~
~~_President Lincoln send a clear message that the American people wanted_~~
~~_slavery to go away? (President Lincoln supported the abolishment of slavery.)_~~


Lincoln had to work very hard to help convince members of Congress to pass
the 13th Amendment, but he would be successful. On January 31, 1865, the
13th Amendment, which abolished slavery, was passed.


There were still millions of slaves outside of the United States. In the islands
of the Caribbean and South America, slaves continued to work on large sugar
plantations in brutal ~~_or terrible_~~ conditions. People continued to be enslaved
in many nations in Asia, Africa, and Europe. But in the United States, slavery
had finally been eliminated.


Unit 7 The U.S. Civil War
**192**


**Show Image 12A-3: Richmond**


Not long after, in the spring of 1865, the Civil
War was finally coming to a close.



On April 1 and 2 of that year, General Ulysses
S. Grant and Union troops won major victories
in Virginia. Here, they cut off the Confederate
supply lines ~~_or stopped the Confederates_~~
~~_from receiving important shipments of items like food, medicine, and_~~
~~_weapons, which they needed to be successful._~~ General Robert E. Lee and his
Confederate troops were forced to abandon the city of Richmond, Virginia,
which was the capital of the Confederacy. ~~[Display the U.S. Map, and point~~
~~out Virginia. Then direct students’ attention to the image of Richmond in~~
~~ruins.]~~





For the next week, Lee and his army retreated ~~_or pulled back to escape a_~~
~~_battle._~~ They were trying to find desperately needed food and supplies while
avoiding the Union Army. Lee’s Confederate soldiers were hungry, tired, and
weary. Some didn’t follow instructions and went searching for food.


**Show Image 12A-4: Appomattox**
**Surrender**



Defeat of the Confederate Army was all but
certain. Grant sent Lee a letter on April 7,
1865, asking Lee to surrender. Lee refused.
Lee thought that he just needed to make it to a
place called Appomattox before Grant’s troops
did. Then, he could resupply his army.



Support


Use a map of Virginia to
demonstrate the distance
between Richmond and
Appomattox.


Challenge


Invite students to discuss
why Appomattox is often
considered the end of the
war, even though it took
months for the rest of
the Confederate forces to
surrender.





But, the Union troops took shorter roads and arrived at Appomattox first.
Now, Lee’s army was trapped and couldn’t escape. Rather than risk the lives
of his weary men, Lee’s only choice was to surrender. On April 9, General
Robert E. Lee and his 28,000 Confederate troops surrendered to General
Grant in Appomattox, Virginia. ~~[Point out General Lee and General Grant in~~
~~the image, depicting the surrender.]~~


It would take many months for the rest of the Confederate forces to
surrender. But the Confederate capital and highest-ranking Confederate
general had been defeated. The surrender at Appomattox was so important
that many people think of it as the end of the war.



Lesson 12 The End of Slavery in the United States
**193**


**Show Image 12A-5: President Lincoln**


After four years and hundreds of thousands
of lives, the Civil War preserved the Union. It
prevented the “house divided” that Abraham
Lincoln had talked about from breaking apart
forever. It brought slavery to an end but at
great cost.



Many people played a role, but none as big as Lincoln. The war had aged him
like it did Lee. He wanted what was best for millions of people and it was a
heavy burden. ~~_Why do you think the war aged Lincoln?_~~ Through it all, Lincoln
stayed true to his moral beliefs informed by the Christian Bible, that he was
a humble servant who made mistakes like any man. ~~_What does it mean to be_~~
~~_humble?_~~


Lincoln once said, “I know that the Lord is always on the side of the right. But
it is my constant anxiety and prayer that I and this nation should be on the
Lord’s side.” As the war progressed, Lincoln believed that God wanted slavery
to end. He believed God wanted to use the Union to make it happen. Lincoln’s
determination, bravery, and leadership led to the end of slavery. ~~_How do you_~~
~~_think Lincoln showed determination to end slavery?_~~ ~~T~~ he Civil War was won by
the Union in 1865.


Former slaves were free and the Union remained intact. Our great nation
survived. After enduring years of loss and devastation, Americans looked
toward a hopeful future.


**Show Image 12A-6: John Wilkes Booth**
**Flees After Attacking President Lincoln**





But on the night of April 14, just five days after
Lee surrendered to Grant, tragedy struck
again. That evening, President Abraham
Lincoln went to watch a play at Ford’s Theater
in Washington, D.C.



Not everyone was happy that the Union emerged victorious ~~_or won_~~ the
Civil War. This included an actor, John Wilkes Booth. He wanted to save the
Confederacy. So, Booth and a group of helpers hatched ~~_or came up with_~~ a
plan to get rid of Lincoln.


During the show, Lincoln was in a cheerful mood. He laughed during the
performance while seated in a private box ~~_or a small separate seating area_~~
~~_for audience members in a theater_~~ with his wife and friends.


Unit 7 The U.S. Civil War
**194**


As the show continued, Booth snuck into Lincoln’s box. He attacked the
president of the United States. ~~[Point out Lincoln’s private box in the~~
~~illustration, along with Booth running away across the stage.]~~ Lincoln was
carried across the street to a boarding house. The surgeon general ~~_or a high-_~~
~~_ranking doctor appointed by the president_~~ arrived to help, but Lincoln would
not survive. The next morning, President Lincoln died, surrounded by his wife
and several of his loved ones.


**Show Image 12A-7: Walt Whitman**



Americans across the country mourned ~~_or_~~
~~_expressed deep sadness about_~~ the death of
their heroic leader. They remembered Lincoln
who bravely led the United States through the
devastating Civil War. As part of a long funeral,

in Illinois. ~~[Point out Illinois on the U.S. Map.]~~
~~_Why would Lincoln’s final resting place be in Illinois? (He was from Illinois.)_~~
Tens of thousands of Americans stood beside the railroad tracks. They
gathered to show respect for the fallen president.





This devastating tragedy inspired the poet Walt Whitman ~~[Point to the~~
~~illustration of Walt Whitman]~~ to write many poems that honor Lincoln’s life,
legacy, and impact. Like Lincoln, Whitman came from humble beginnings.
Whitman recognized the immense ~~_or huge_~~ burden that Lincoln carried to
save the Union.


Whitman spent time writing poems to remember Lincoln’s life and memory.
Published in the Saturday Press on November 4, 1865, “O Captain! My
Captain!” became one of Whitman’s most famous poems.


The poem reflects the mixed emotions of Americans at the time of Lincoln’s
death. The Union had endured a devastating ~~_or deeply upsetting_~~ conflict,
won the Civil War, and ended slavery. There was much to celebrate. There
was also much to mourn. ~~_Can you recall what_~~ ~~mourn~~ ~~_means?_~~ Not only was
Lincoln gone, but many Americans had lost loved ones in the Civil War.


“O Captain! My Captain!” captures these contrasting feelings of sadness and
joy, despair and relief.


The poem clearly struck a chord ~~_or affected emotions_~~ within the hearts of the
American people. It honored the contributions of Lincoln. It also expressed the
confusing emotions that Americans were feeling after the Civil War ended. But
the sacrifices of those who led, fought, contributed, and experienced hardship

**195**


and loss will always be remembered. This is why we learn about the Civil War—
because of the contributions of all of these people that we have learned about.
People like President Lincoln, Harriet Tubman, General Grant, Clara Barton,
and Frederick Douglass helped make sure that slavery ended in America.
Today, every man, woman, and child, no matter the color of their skin, can live

~~**COMPREHENSION QUESTIONS (10 MIN.)**~~


1. **Literal.** Who played the biggest role in the successful end of the Civil War and

the elimination of slavery in the United States?


» President Lincoln


2. **Inferential.** Why did the end of the Civil War cause Americans to look toward

a hopeful future?


» The end of the war meant that slavery was abolished in the country, and

the Confederate states were brought back into the Union to begin the
process of moving toward a unified and stronger country.


3. **Inferential.** In the Read-Aloud, you heard that Walt Whitman recognized the

huge burden that President Lincoln carried to save the Union; what was the
burden he carried?


» President Lincoln had to go to war against the Confederacy and

sacrifice hundreds of thousands of lives to end slavery and reunite the
nation.


4. **Inferential.** Why would Whitman refer to President Lincoln as a “captain” in

his poem “O Captain! My Captain!”?


» Whitman may have referred to President Lincoln as a captain because

he was a respected leader in charge of “steering the ship” during the
Civil War, much like a captain.


5. **Evaluative.** _Think-Pair-Share:_ In the poem “O Captain! My Captain!,” Walt

Whitman says that even though the “captain” has died, “the prize we [looked
for] is won.” What “prize” do you think he is talking about?


» Answers may vary, but students will likely identify possible “prizes” as

the abolishment of slavery, the end of the violence, or the reunification
of the country.

~~**WORD WORK: AMENDMENT (5 MIN.)**~~


1. In the Read-Aloud you heard, “Lincoln had to work very hard to help convince
members of Congress to pass the 13th Amendment, but he would be
successful.”


2. Say the word _amendment_ with me.


3. An amendment is a change or an update to something that has already been
established, usually an official document. In this case, an amendment is
specifically a change or an update to the U.S. Constitution.


4. The First _Amendment_ provides Americans with the freedom of speech.


5. What’s the word we’ve been talking about?


Lesson 12 The End of Slavery in the United States
**197**


**Use a Making Choices activity for follow-up.** You have heard that an
amendment most often refers to changes or updates in official documents,
such as the U.S. Constitution. The word _amend_ is a variation that means
to change or improve, and it can be used when someone makes a change
or correction to anything, not just an official document. I am going to read
several sentences. If the person has decided to change or correct something,
say, “_____ amended something.” If the person does not change or update
something, say, “_____ did not amend something.”


                 - Darrell’s sister asked for chocolate ice cream, then decided she would rather
have vanilla.


» Darrell’s sister amended her ice cream flavor choice.


                 - Darla told her friends she would join the soccer team, and she did.


» Darla did not amend her decision to join the soccer team.


                 - Last night Billy’s mother promised him he could stay home from school, but

this morning she said he had to go in case there was a test.


» Billy’s mother amended her decision about going to school.


                 - Lisa told her brother he could borrow her favorite sweater, but when he

asked for it, she told him she might want to wear it, and he would have to find
something else.


» Lisa amended her decision to lend her brother her sweater.


                - My grandfather promised me he would take me fishing, and even though it

rained, we went and caught four big fish.


» My grandfather did not amend his promise to take me fishing.

**Grade 2 Unit 7**
#### Unit Review


~~**NOTE TO TEACHER**~~


You should spend one day reviewing and reinforcing the material in this unit.
You may have students do any combination of the activities provided, in either
whole-group or small-group settings.


~~**CORE CONTENT OBJECTIVES ADDRESSED IN THIS UNIT**~~


**Students will:**

                 - Describe what slavery is and identify examples of it throughout global history.


                - Explain what the Great Awakenings were and what many Founding Fathers
came to believe about slavery.


                 - Describe what the abolitionists believed about slavery and what influenced

them.


                 - Identify the Underground Railroad as a system of escape for slaves in the
United States.


                 - Describe the life and contributions of Harriet Tubman.


                - Identify the differences between the Northern and Southern economies
leading up to the Civil War.


                 - Describe Abraham Lincoln’s beliefs about slavery.


                 - Explain the conflicts between the North and South that led to the Civil War.


                 - Explain how the “Battle Hymn of the Republic” inspired Union soldiers to keep

fighting.


                - Explain the importance of the Emancipation Proclamation.


                - Explain why President Lincoln is remembered as a courageous president.


                 - Describe the life and contributions of Clara Barton.


                 - Describe the similarities and differences between the Union and Confederate
armies.


                 - Describe the similarities and differences between Robert E. Lee and Ulysses S.
Grant.


                - Summarize the costs and outcomes of the Civil War.


                 - Describe Abraham Lincoln’s role in ending slavery in the United States.


Unit 7 The U.S. Civil War
**202**


~~**REVIEW ACTIVITIES**~~


**Riddles for Core Content**

 - Ask students riddles such as the following to review core content:


   - I was the commander in chief of the Union Army. Who am I?

_(Abraham Lincoln)_


   - My nickname was “The Old Man,” and I led the Confederate Army.

Who am I? (General Robert E. Lee)


   - I helped gather medical supplies for the wounded soldiers and was

nicknamed “Angel of the Battlefield.” Who am I? _(Clara Barton)_


   - I was an important announcement from President Lincoln that changed the

focus of the war to slavery. What am I called? _(Emancipation Proclamation)_


   - I commanded the Union Army and demanded “unconditional surrender”

from the Confederates. Who am I? _(General Ulysses S. Grant)_


   - We fought together to pressure political leaders to end slavery.

Who are we? _(abolitionists)_


   - I was a conductor on the Underground Railroad and used the North Star to

navigate escaped slaves to safety. Who am I? _(Harriet Tubman)_


   - I am the song written by Julia Ward Howe that helped inspire the Union

soldiers to keep fighting. What am I called? _(“Battle Hymn of_
_the Republic”)_


**Image Review**

 - Show the Flip Book images from any Read-Aloud again, and have students
retell the Read-Aloud using the images.


**Image Card Review**

 - Option 1: Pass out image cards 6–13, used for the timeline, to eight students.
Have them arrange the cards to show the correct sequence.


 - Option 2: Help the class identify all of the image cards. Then pass them out
to various students. Have one student stand and identify their image. Ask any
other students who think their card is connected to join the person standing
and then explain the connection. For example, if the first person had the
card for Abraham Lincoln, the person with the card for the Emancipation
Proclamation could join them and explain that Abraham Lincoln wrote the
Emancipation Proclamation.


 - Option 3: Help students identify all of the image cards and brainstorm what
has been learned about each. Then give students the various image cards.
